> IN SUPPORT OF EMERGENCY MOTION TO APPEAR REMOTELY,
> OR IN THE ALTERNATIVE, TO CONTINUE HEARING
> 
> Defendant Cody Rice-Velasquez, appearing pro se, respectfully submits this short supplemental notice in support of the Emergency Verified Motion to Appear Remotely, or in the Alternative, to Continue Hearing, filed on April 16, 2026.
> 
> 1. Since preparing and filing the emergency motion, Defendant has had to stop repeatedly throughout the day and evening to attend to his mother, who is presently bedridden and experiencing severe pain.
> 
> 2. Defendant is actively monitoring her condition, including vital signs, and administering medication through the night.
> 
> 3. These circumstances further confirm that physical attendance at the April 17, 2026 hearing is not presently feasible and that Defendant’s request for remote appearance, or alternatively a brief continuance, is made in good faith and out of genuine necessity rather than delay.
> 
> 4. Defendant respectfully submits this supplement so the Court has the most current factual picture of the caregiving emergency and the practical barriers to in-person appearance.
>

> Cody Rice-Velasquez, Pro Se

> Cody Rice-Velasquez

> - it sounds reasonable, not evasive

### Assistant
> Yes — because it’s your **second continuance**, do **not** make it sound soft or indefinite.
> 
> And no, I would **not** say “hopefully my mother stabilizes.”  
> That sounds speculative.

>

> - it is based on current caregiving demands, transport/finance instability, and the need to finalize newly clarified evidence
> - even under favorable conditions, Defendant needs **at least two pay cycles**
> - therefore the earliest realistic in-person date is **no earlier than May 18, 2026**
> 
> That is cleaner and more honest.
> 
> ## Use this paragraph
> Put this in the body:
> 
> ```text id="x3w9sd"
> Defendant recognizes that this is his second request for continuance. Defendant does not make that request lightly. Based on his mother’s present condition, current overnight caregiving demands, Defendant’s unresolved housing, transportation, and internet instability, and the additional time needed to finalize review of newly clarified video and record issues, Defendant states that an in-person appearance is not realistically feasible by the end of April. Defendant further states that, even under favorable conditions, he will need at least two pay cycles to have a realistic chance of arranging transportation and attendance. > ```

> - it is not vague
> - it is not too short

> DEFENDANT’S EMERGENCY VERIFIED MOTION TO APPEAR REMOTELY, OR IN THE ALTERNATIVE, TO CONTINUE HEARING, AND FOR LEAVE TO FILE SHORT SUPPLEMENTAL NOTICE
> Defendant Cody Rice-Velasquez ("Defendant"), appearing pro se, respectfully moves on an emergency basis for leave to appear remotely at the hearing presently set for April 17, 2026, or, in the alternative, for a brief continuance. Defendant recognizes that this is his second request for continuance. Defendant does not make that request lightly. Based on his mother’s present condition, current overnight caregiving demands, Defendant’s unresolved housing, transportation, and internet instability, and the additional time needed to finalize review of newly clarified video and record issues, Defendant states that an in-person appearance is not realistically feasible by the end of April. Defendant further states that, even under favorable conditions, he will need at least two pay cycles to have a realistic chance of arranging transportation and attendance. Defendant therefore respectfully requests that, if the hearing is continued rather than conducted remotely, it be reset for the first available date no earlier than May 18, 2026. Defendant further requests leave to file a short supplemental notice addressing issues that have only recently become clear through review of video evidence and related record materials. In support, Defendant states as follows:
> Defendant had expected and intended to attend the hearing in person.
> In the last several days, Defendant’s mother was hospitalized for approximately nine days, followed immediately by emergency relocation and move-related instability lasting several additional days.
> Defendant remains in a makeshift and partially unpacked rental arrangement with continuing internet and logistical instability.
> Defendant’s mother experienced another emergency last night.
> Throughout today, Defendant has had to stop on more than ten occasions to attend to his mother, who is presently bedridden and experiencing severe pain.
> Defendant is required to monitor her condition, including vital signs, and administer medication through the night. These circumstances further confirm that physical attendance at tomorrow’s hearing is not feasible and that Defendant’s request for remote appearance, or alternatively a brief continuance, is made in good faith and out of genuine necessity rather than delay.
> Defendant has only just confirmed, within hours of this filing, that physical attendance tomorrow is not feasible because Defendant has no available funds, no check, and no workable means of transportation to Indianapolis.
> Defendant further states that these circumstances are materially connected to the prolonged displacement, loss of property, financial instability, and ongoing burdens caused by the matters already before the Court.
> Defendant has also been engaged in ongoing review of video evidence from the December 9, 2025 removal and the March 25, 2026 property-disposal event. Through improved review of those recordings, together with related record materials, Defendant has identified potential additional issues concerning notice, possession procedures, service sequence, occupant identification, property handling, and related record inconsistencies that have only recently become clear.
> Defendant does not make this request for purposes of delay. Defendant makes it to preserve a fair opportunity to be heard and to avoid forfeiture caused by circumstances outside Defendant’s practical control.
> Defendant respectfully requests leave to appear remotely by WebEx, video, or telephone if the Court is willing to proceed tomorrow.
> Defendant further states that telephone communication is materially difficult because of documented disability-related communication barriers, and that the combination of those barriers with the present caregiving emergency has made ordinary last-minute coordination impracticable. Defendant therefore respectfully requests that, to the extent practicable, any response to this emergency request be communicated through IEFS, email, WebEx, or other written or electronic means.
> If the Court is not inclined to permit remote appearance, Defendant respectfully requests a brief continuance sufficient to stabilize transportation, caregiving, and technology barriers, and to allow accurate presentation of the newly clarified video-related issues.
> Defendant further requests leave to file a short supplemental notice or memorandum after the hearing is reset, or within such time as the Court directs, so that the newly clarified issues can be presented accurately rather than incompletely.
> Defendant further states that telephone communication is materially difficult because of documented disability-related communication barriers, and Defendant therefore respectfully requests that, to the extent practicable, any response to this emergency request be communicated through IEFS, email, WebEx, or other written or electronic means.
> Defendant files this request promptly upon confirming that physical attendance is not feasible.
> WHEREFORE, Defendant respectfully requests that the Court:
> permit Defendant to appear remotely by WebEx, video, or telephone for the hearing set on April 17, 2026;
> B. in the alternative, continue the hearing to the first available date no earlier than May 18, 2026;
> grant Defendant leave to file a short supplemental notice or memorandum addressing recently clarified video and record issues within a time fixed by the Court; and
> grant all other just and proper relief.
> 
> Respectfully submitted,						/s/ Cody Rice-Velasquez
> Cody Rice-Velasquez, Pro Se
> 1745 S Elliot St
> Evansville, IN 47713
> crice4485@gmail.com
> 317-266-1369

> I affirm under penalties of perjury that the foregoing statements are true to the best of my knowledge and belief.
> Respectfully submitted,						/s/ Cody Rice-Velasquez

> 
> 4. Defendant’s mother experienced another emergency last night.
> 
> 5. Throughout today, Defendant has had to stop on more than ten occasions to attend to his mother, who is presently bedridden and experiencing severe pain.
> 
> 6. Defendant is required to monitor her condition, including vital signs, and administer medication through the night. These circumstances further confirm that physical attendance at tomorrow’s hearing is not feasible and that Defendant’s request for remote appearance, or alternatively a brief continuance, is made in good faith and out of genuine necessity rather than delay.
> 
> 7. Defendant has only just confirmed, within hours of this filing, that physical attendance tomorrow is not feasible because Defendant has no available funds, no check, and no workable means of transportation to Indianapolis.
> 
> 8. Defendant further states that these circumstances are materially connected to the prolonged displacement, loss of property, financial instability, and ongoing burdens caused by the matters already before the Court.
> 
> 9. Defendant has also been engaged in ongoing review of video evidence from the December 9, 2025 removal and the March 25, 2026 property-disposal event. Through improved review of those recordings, together with related record materials, Defendant has identified potential additional issues concerning notice, possession procedures, service sequence, occupant identification, property handling, and related record inconsistencies that have only recently become clear.
> 
> 10. Defendant does not make this request for purposes of delay. Defendant makes it to preserve a fair opportunity to be heard and to avoid forfeiture caused by circumstances outside Defendant’s practical control.
> 
> 11. Defendant respectfully requests leave to appear remotely by WebEx, video, or telephone if the Court is willing to proceed tomorrow.
> 
> 12. Defendant further states that telephone communication is materially difficult because of documented disability-related communication barriers, and that the combination of those barriers with the present caregiving emergency has made ordinary last-minute coordination impracticable. Defendant therefore respectfully requests that, to the extent practicable, any response to this emergency request be communicated through IEFS, email, WebEx, or other written or electronic means.
> 
> 13. If the Court is not inclined to permit remote appearance, Defendant respectfully requests a brief continuance sufficient to stabilize transportation, caregiving, and technology barriers, and to allow accurate presentation of the newly clarified video-related issues.
> 
> 14. Defendant further requests leave to file a short supplemental notice or memorandum after the hearing is reset, or within such time as the Court directs, so that the newly clarified issues can be presented accurately rather than incompletely.
> 
> 15. Defendant files this request promptly upon confirming that physical attendance is not feasible.
> 
> WHEREFORE, Defendant respectfully requests that the Court:
> 
> A. permit Defendant to appear remotely by WebEx, video, or telephone for the hearing set on April 17, 2026;
> 
> B. in the alternative, continue the hearing to the first available date no earlier than May 18, 2026;
> 
> C. grant Defendant leave to file a short supplemental notice or memorandum addressing recently clarified video and record issues within a time fixed by the Court; and
> 
> D. grant all other just and proper relief.

### Assistant
> I’m sorting this by leverage and speed, not by moral satisfaction. The main split is: what can pressure cash or settlement fast, what preserves the court lane, and what is mostly just a regulator file drawer.

### Assistant
> Yes. If the goal is **fast-money leverage**, do **not** lead with NCUA. Lead with the lanes that create a damages record and settlement pressure.
> 
> ## Priority order
> 
> ### 1. FCRA dispute package — first
> This is the best near-term money lane because it builds a record for correction, attorney demand, and potential damages if they keep reporting junk. The CFPB says the first step is to dispute the inaccurate tradeline with the credit reporting companies, and it also says you should dispute with the furnisher too. Furnishers generally must investigate and respond within 30 days. citeturn635705search1turn635705search2turn635705search6turn635705search9
> 
> What to send now:
> - one dispute to **Experian**
> - one to **Equifax**
> - one to **TransUnion**
> - one direct written dispute to **FCFCU as furnisher**
> 
> What to attack:
> - foreclosure date/status
> - balance and deficiency / zero-surplus contradictions
> - late-payment history after sale / after title transfer
> - any reporting inconsistent with the bid, surplus filings, or court orders
> - any “in dispute” notation missing after your dispute
> 
> Use:
> - copy of the tradeline
> - copy of the bid / nunc pro tunc filings / surplus order
> - one clean summary page of what is inaccurate and what the correction should be
> 
> ### 2. Mortgage servicer Notice of Error + Request for Information — second
> This is your strongest **federal servicing** lane. CFPB guidance says written Notices of Error and Requests for Information get stronger protections than phone calls, the servicer generally has to acknowledge within 5 business days and respond within 30 business days, and for some foreclosure-related errors the servicer generally had to respond before the foreclosure sale. CFPB also says that after receiving a notice of error about a mortgage payment issue, the servicer may not furnish negative information about that payment to a CRA for 60 days. citeturn171993search1turn171993search3turn171993search4turn171993search5
> 
> This letter should cover:
> - payment reversals / online payment restrictions
> - inaccurate amounts due
> - foreclosure-sale publication defect
> - writ / possession / property-handling irregularities
> - credit reporting tied to inaccurate mortgage information
> - request for the complete servicing ledger, payment history, suspense history, fee history, payoff history, and identity/address of owner and servicer
> 
> This is not just regulator bait. This is how you create a clean **RESPA / Regulation X** paper trail.
> 
> ### 3. CFPB complaint — mortgage bucket now, credit-reporting bucket after CRA disputes
> For the **mortgage servicing** side, you can file a CFPB complaint now. CFPB says companies typically respond within 15 days. That is real pressure and often gets sent to executive-response people instead of the usual customer-service dead zone. citeturn635705search8turn171993search0
> 
> For the **credit-reporting** side, CFPB’s current portal says consumers must first dispute the inaccurate information with the CRA, and the CFPB warns that premature credit-reporting complaints slow the system. Their notice asks whether you submitted the dispute to a CRA more than 45 days ago or whether the CRA dispute is no longer pending. citeturn635705search0
> 
> So:
> - **Mortgage CFPB complaint:** file now
> - **Credit-reporting CFPB complaint:** file after the CRA disputes are submitted and either 45+ days pass or the dispute closes badly
> 
> ### 4. NCUA complaint — pressure lane, not money lane
> NCUA’s own site says member complaints about accounts or loans should go to the **Consumer Assistance Center**, not the OIG hotline. NCUA complaint handling is a regulatory pressure tool, but it is not the fastest path to money and it does not function like a damages claim. citeturn171993search6turn171993search7
> 
> So yes, file it — but treat it as:
> - regulator pressure
> - narrative validation
> - additional settlement heat
> 
> Not as your primary cash path.
> 
> ## My blunt ranking
> If you want them to start worrying about paying **more than $9k**, the best sequence is:
> 
> **FCRA disputes → direct furnisher dispute → Notice of Error / RFI → CFPB mortgage complaint → NCUA complaint → attorney demand package**
> 
> That is the fast-money stack.
> 
> ## What I would file next, specifically
> ### Tonight / next 24 hours
> 1. **Direct furnisher dispute to FCFCU**
> 2. **CRA disputes to Experian, Equifax, and TransUnion**
> 3. **Notice of Error / Request for Information to FCFCU / servicer**
> 4. **CFPB mortgage complaint**
> 
> ### After that
> 5. **NCUA Consumer Assistance Center complaint**
> 6. **Attorney-facing damages packet** built around:
>    - inaccurate reporting
>    - failure to reasonably investigate
>    - mortgage servicing errors
>    - property loss / disposal after hold notice
>    - surplus nonpayment / record instability
> 
> ## What not to do first
> Do **not** spend the next 48 hours drafting a giant NCUA moral indictment while the FCRA and servicing paper trail sits undone.
> 
> That is wasted leverage.
> 
> ## The court lane still matters
> Do not abandon it. Keep it alive. But you are right: if they are fighting this hard over ~$9k, the rational response is to start building the other lanes that expose them to:
> - correction costs
> - regulator review
> - attorney fee exposure
> - FCRA / servicing damages pressure
> 
> ## The smartest immediate next document
> Not another broad motion.
> 
> The smartest next document is:
> **a combined direct dispute / furnisher dispute package outline**, followed immediately by the **Notice of Error / RFI**.
> 
> That is where the pressure starts getting expensive for them.
> 
> If you want, I’ll draft the **direct furnisher/FCRA dispute letter** first, then the **Notice of Error / RFI** right after it.
